## [7/603] Issue with Missing UBID
Source: gmail | Thread: 19d52fdf13c8b0bd | Relevance: 9/10 | Mention: direct | Labels: production-incident, ad-tracking, vendor-escalation, data-integrity, architecture-review | People: Rahul Jain, Michael Bui, Nikhil Grover
Vendor Osmos (Rahul Jain) flagged a critical production issue where the client fails to send the User ID (UBID) in the 'uclid' parameter for AppsFlyer tracking events. Logs from April 1, 2026, confirm that this results in 'DUMMY_UBID' assignments, corrupting funnel impression tracking data for Brand Ads and impacting Retail Media integrity.

Michael Bui was explicitly addressed alongside Nikhil Grover to resolve this. While Nikhil sought clarification on ad unit types (display vs. product), Michael took the lead by requesting specific definitions for UBID/uclid, the associated customer journey/platform details, and the full scope of impact. This requires Michael's architectural judgment to determine if the root cause is an event configuration error or a deeper API integration gap requiring code changes.

Action Required: Michael must clarify the technical mapping with Osmos and coordinate a fix for the event configuration to ensure valid user identification in the ad stack.

## [20/603] Re: [## 112603 ##] Sev1 incident: Ad Products per response is low for PLA
Source: gmail | Thread: 19d2ead5d3ae56a5 | Relevance: 9/10 | Mention: direct | Labels: sev1-incident, pladelivery-fix, vendor-collaboration, configuration-correction, architect-guidance | Work Items: [## 112603 ##] | People: Michael Bui, Nikhil Grover
This thread documents the resolution of Sev1 incident [## 112603 ##], where Programmatic Listing Ads (PLA) were returning fewer products than expected due to an incorrect 'pcnt' parameter value. The root cause was identified as the parameter defaulting to '1' instead of the required '6'. Michael Bui was explicitly tagged by Nikhil Grover on March 27th to provide technical guidance and assist with request URL verification for Osmos Support. Although Osmos requested specific URLs for deep analysis on March 31st, the FPG engineering team successfully identified and resolved the issue internally by updating configurations to ensure 'pcnt = 6' is passed for all PLA requests. The fix was implemented by 3 PM Singapore time on March 31st, with Osmos Support confirming the correct configuration on April 1st. Michael's involvement was critical in bridging vendor requirements and internal implementation standards.

## [84/603] Trivy compromise & LiteLLM infected
Source: gmail | Thread: 19d2d713065f8bdf | Relevance: 9/10 | Mention: indirect | Labels: security-advisory, supply-chain, remediation-action, credential-risk, ai-governance | People: Nicholas Tan
Critical security advisory regarding supply chain compromises in Trivy (v0.69.4) and LiteLLM (v1.82.7/8). The compromised Trivy version inadvertently infected the LiteLLM package distribution, posing a high risk of credential exfiltration. Michael Bui must act immediately due to his dual mandate in Platform Architecture and AI governance.

Required Actions:
1. Verify local Trivy installation: Run `trivy --version`. If v0.69.4, send output to the forensic team.
2. Remediation: Uninstall via `brew uninstall trivy` (or equivalent) and reinstall safe version v0.69.3 using `brew install trivy`.
3. Verify LiteLLM: Run `pip show litellm | grep Version`. Report if version is 1.82.7 or 1.82.8.

Cluster scans currently show no infected images, but local developer environments remain at risk. Immediate reporting to the Tech Infra and CyberSecurity teams is mandatory.

Michael Bui directly owns and executed the resolution of Jira ticket DPD-700 to address Low and Informational security findings from an RMN pentest. On March 9, he created the ticket, and by March 10 at 10:36 AM SGT, he completed all necessary infrastructure changes and marked the task as Done.

Key actions taken:
- **Security Headers**: Configured HSTS (max-age=31536000), CSP (default-src 'none'), X-Content-Type-Options (nosiff), X-Frame-Options (DENY), Referrer-Policy, and Cache-Control (no-store) on the `marketing-personalization-service` in both Preproduction and Production.
- **Rate Limiting**: Deployed Cloud Armor rate limiting set to 200 requests per second per IP with a 429 deny response upon exceedance.
- **Status Update**: Issues related to TLS vulnerabilities (SWEET32, BEAST) were previously resolved via GCP SSL Policy. The CORS wildcard issue remains 'Accepted' as it requires application-level code changes.

This is a high-priority engagement where Michael successfully validated SLO compliance through header verification and managed the end-to-end release workflow.

Jira ticket DPD-715 outlines a feature to enable dynamic ad slot configuration on the Omni homepage swimlanes via Split feature flags. This allows Product Managers to adjust ad count and positions (e.g., [3, 5, 7]) without code changes, handling scenarios like fallback defaults, density adjustments, empty states, supply shortages, and out-of-bounds indices.
